## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through constitutive laws (elastic, plastic, or viscoplastic) and temperature typically causes thermal softening of material properties.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic stress-strain curve)
- Johnson-Cook strength model (static): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (coupled strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (nonlinear elastoplastic with saturation)
- Voce hardening law: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (exponential saturation hardening)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermal softening linear: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (modulus linearly decreasing with temperature)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power law with pre-strain offset)
- Exponential thermal softening with power hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal factor with strain hardening)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (Taylor expansion of constitutive law)
- Hyperbolic sine flow rule: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon) (hot deformation creep-type model)
- Zener-Hollomon inspired: sigma = c0 * log(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T) + 1) (logarithmic stress with thermally activated deformation)
- Bilinear with thermal coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) + c2 * T (linear strain and temperature terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T**n) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress at higher temperatures
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), or Voce-type forms
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 indicates work hardening in metals
- Additive yield stress + hardening → Constant term c0 plus strain-dependent term models initial yield followed by hardening
- Coupled strain-temperature effects → Multiplicative decomposition: f(epsilon) * g(T) separates mechanical and thermal contributions
- Logarithmic stress dependence → log(1 + c*epsilon) or arcsinh(c*epsilon) for rate/strain sensitivity at large deformations
- Pre-strain offset in power law → (epsilon + c)**n instead of epsilon**n avoids singularity at zero strain and models prior deformation history
- Temperature-dependent modulus → Young's modulus as polynomial or exponential function of T multiplied by strain

## GT Analysis

The GT expression is:
```

```

Expanding the first term:
```

```

Since c3 = 1: `c0*epsilon - c0*c1*epsilon*δT = c0*epsilon - c0*c1*epsilon*T + c0*c1*c2*epsilon`

So the first term = `(c0 + c0*c1*c2)*epsilon - c0*c1*epsilon*T` = `A*epsilon - B*epsilon*T` where A, B are constants.

The second term: `c4*epsilon**c5*exp(-c6/(c7*T))` — this has an exponential of -1/T form (Arrhenius-like).

The third term: `c9*epsilon**c8*(T - c10)` = `c9*epsilon**c8*T - c9*c10*epsilon**c8` = `c9*T*epsilon**c8 - c9*c10*epsilon**c8`

1. `T*epsilon` (linear in T, linear in epsilon)
2. `epsilon` (constant coefficient)

The critical distinguishing feature is the **Arrhenius term** `exp(-c/(T))`. This is NOT equivalent to any polynomial, power law, or simple exponential in T.

### Candidate 6:

T*c0*epsilon + T**c1*c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*epsilon + c6*epsilon**c7
```
Has T**c1 term. If c1=1, this becomes (c0+c2)*T*epsilon + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*epsilon + c6*epsilon**c7. No Arrhenius term.

Could T**c1 somehow approximate exp(-c/T)? No - T**c1*epsilon is a power law in T, not exp(-c/T). These are fundamentally different functions.

Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 7:
```
T*c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*exp(T*c5) + c6*epsilon**c7 + c8*epsilon
```
Has exp(T*c5) but this is exp(aT), not exp(-c/T). These are different. Also, exp(T*c5) doesn't depend on epsilon, while the GT's Arrhenius term does (through epsilon**c5).

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 8:
```
T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*epsilon + c6*epsilon**c2
```
This has: T*epsilon, T*epsilon**c2, epsilon**c4, epsilon, epsilon**c2. No Arrhenius term.

But wait - GT has terms: T*epsilon, epsilon, T*epsilon^1.45, epsilon^1.45, epsilon^0.318*exp(-5.95/T).

This candidate has T*epsilon, T*epsilon**c2, epsilon**c4, epsilon, epsilon**c2. If c2≈1.45, c4≈0.318, this matches 4 of the 5 GT terms but misses the Arrhenius factor on the epsilon^0.318 term. The candidate has c3*epsilon**c4 (pure power law) while GT has epsilon^0.318*exp(-5.95/T) (power law × Arrhenius). These cannot be equal.

Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 9:
```
T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon/(c7+epsilon)
```
No Arrhenius term.

Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 10:

```
No Arrhenius term. Just polynomials/powers of epsilon with linear T dependence.

Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Has exp(c4*epsilon) - exponential in epsilon, not exp(-c/T). No Arrhenius term.

Candidate 14 verdict: [NO MATCH]

However, let me think more carefully. Could exp(T*c7*epsilon**c8) somehow match? The GT has epsilon^0.318*exp(-5.95/T). These are fundamentally different: one grows exponentially with T, the other decays. They cannot be equal.

## Summary

None of the candidates contain the essential Arrhenius-type term `exp(-c/T)` that appears in the GT. All exponential terms in the candidates are of the form `exp(aT)`, `exp(aT*epsilon^b)`, or `exp(a*epsilon)`, which are fundamentally different from `exp(-c/T)`.
